Introduction

Scholars@TAMU is a profile system that hosts searchable expertise for faculty and TAMU organizations by gathering data from institution-level/enterprise systems, publicly available research data (e.g., grants and publications), and other authoritative sources. The data is compiled into a profile that you can edit to best represent your scholarship and expertise.

This system helps to:

  • Improve the discoverability of scholarly expertise

  • Enhance the scholarly identity of researchers

  • Facilitate new research collaborations.

1. Discovery

1.1. Collections

1.1.1. Directory

This provides a directory listing view of all the collections present in the system, based on the request parameters as shown.

Request Parameters
Parameter Description

+page+

The page number.

+size+

The page size.

+sort+

The page sort [field,asc/desc].
Response Fields
Path Type Description

+_embedded.collections+

+Array+

An array of Collection resources.

+_links+

+Object+

Links to other resources.

+page+

+Object+

Page details for Collection resources.

+facets+

+Array+

Facets for Collection resources.
Sample Request
GET /collections?page=0&size=20&sort=id HTTP/1.1
Host: localhost:8080
Sample Response
HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Pragma: no-cache
X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
Expires: 0
X-Frame-Options: DENY
X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
Content-Type: application/hal+json;charset=UTF-8
Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, max-age=0, must-revalidate
Content-Length: 9213

1.1.2. Find By Id

This will find a concept based on the concept id provided as a parameter as shown in Path Parameters. The json response will have the specific concept as shown in the Sample Response.

Path Parameters
Table 1. /collections/{id}
Parameter Description

+id+

The Collection id.
Sample Request
GET /collections/n0166-4328ISSN HTTP/1.1
Host: localhost:8080
Sample Response
HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Pragma: no-cache
X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
Expires: 0
X-Frame-Options: DENY
X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
Content-Type: application/hal+json;charset=UTF-8
Content-Length: 4954
Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, max-age=0, must-revalidate

1.1.3. Find By Id In

This will find a list of collections based on the concept ids provided as a parameter as shown in Request Parameters. The json response will have the specific collections as shown in the Sample Response.

Request Parameters
Parameter Description

+ids+

The Collection ids.
Sample Request
GET /collections/search/findByIdIn?ids=n2052-1537ISSN%2Cn0029-6635ISSN%2Cn0166-4328ISSN HTTP/1.1
Host: localhost:8080
Sample Response
HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Pragma: no-cache
Content-Length: 8948
X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
Expires: 0
X-Frame-Options: DENY
X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
Content-Type: application/hal+json;charset=UTF-8
Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, max-age=0, must-revalidate

1.1.4. Search

This search will return a json response listing all the collections, based on the query parameters as shown in Request Parameters.

Request Parameters
Parameter Description

+query+

The search query

+facets+

The facet fields

+type.limit+

Type facet limit

+type.offset+

Type facet offset

+type.sort+

Type facet sort {index/count}

+page+

The page number

+size+

The page size

+sort+

The page sort field,{asc/desc}
Response Fields
Path Type Description

+_embedded.collections+

+Array+

An array of Collection resources.

+_links+

+Object+

Links to other resources.

+page+

+Object+

Page details for Collection resources.

+facets+

+Array+

Facets for Collection resources.

GET /collections/search/facet?query=*&facets=type&type.limit=5&type.offset=0&type.sort=COUNT&page=0&size=20&sort=id HTTP/1.1

1.1.5. Count

This count will return a json response containing the count, based on the query parameters as shown in Request Parameters.

Request Parameters
Parameter Description

+query+

The search query
Response Fields
Path Type Description

+value+

+Number+

The resulting count.
Sample Request
GET /collections/search/count?query=* HTTP/1.1
Host: localhost:8080
Sample Response
HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Pragma: no-cache
X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
Expires: 0
X-Frame-Options: DENY
X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
Content-Length: 17
Content-Type: application/json;charset=UTF-8
Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, max-age=0, must-revalidate

{
  "value" : 3
}
CURL Sample
$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/collections/search/count?query=*' -i -X GET

1.2.4. Search

This search will return a json response listing all the concepts, based on the query parameters as shown in Request Parameters.

Request Parameters
Parameter Description

+query+

The search query

+facets+

The facet fields

+type.limit+

Type facet limit

+type.offset+

Type facet offset

+type.sort+

Type facet sort {index/count}

+page+

The page number

+size+

The page size

+sort+

The page sort field,{asc/desc}
Response Fields
Path Type Description

+_embedded.concepts+

+Array+

An array of Concept resources.

+_links+

+Object+

Links to other resources.

+page+

+Object+

Page details for Concept resources.

+facets+

+Array+

Facets for Concept resources.

{
  "_embedded" : {
    "documents" : [ {
      "id" : "n284161SE",
      "title" : "Cascade industrial VSI gives medium voltage-a case study",
      "type" : [ "ConferencePaper" ],
      "abstract" : "In this paper, the modularity concept applied to medium-voltage adjustable speed drives (MV-ASD) is addressed. First, the single-phase cascaded (SC) VSI that uses series connection of IGBT H-bridge modules with isolated DC-buses is presented. Next, a novel triphase cascaded (TC) VSI that uses three IGBT triphase inverter modules along with an output transformer to obtain a 3 p.u. multilevel output voltage is introduced. The system yields a high-quality multistep voltage with up to 4 levels and low dv/dt, balanced operation of the inverter modules that supply each a third of the motor kVA. The concept of using TC-VSI is further extended to a new modular motor-modular inverter (MM-MI) system where the MV motor winding connections are reconnected into several three-phase groups, either six-lead or twelve-lead connection according to the voltage height, each powered by a standard triphase IGBT inverter module. Thus a high fault-tolerance is being achieved and the output transformer requirement is eliminated. A staggered space vector modulation (SSVM) technique applicable to triphase cascaded VSI topologies is also demonstrated. Both TC-VSI and MM-MI computer simulations and experimental tests demonstrate the feasibility of the systems",

The effect on liver 5'-D was more pronounced with cGH than with a total PD extract, whereas the effect on plasma T3 was somewhat less pronounced. It was concluded that cGH increased the peripheral conversion of T4 into T3 in the chick embryo, whereas a PD extract depleted of cGH was purely thyrotropic. The PD extract also seemed to have 5'-D-suppressing activity.",

      "title" : "Cascade industrial VSI gives medium voltage-a case study",
      "type" : [ "ConferencePaper" ],
      "abstract" : "In this paper, the modularity concept applied to medium-voltage adjustable speed drives (MV-ASD) is addressed. First, the single-phase cascaded (SC) VSI that uses series connection of IGBT H-bridge modules with isolated DC-buses is presented. Next, a novel triphase cascaded (TC) VSI that uses three IGBT triphase inverter modules along with an output transformer to obtain a 3 p.u. multilevel output voltage is introduced. The system yields a high-quality multistep voltage with up to 4 levels and low dv/dt, balanced operation of the inverter modules that supply each a third of the motor kVA. The concept of using TC-VSI is further extended to a new modular motor-modular inverter (MM-MI) system where the MV motor winding connections are reconnected into several three-phase groups, either six-lead or twelve-lead connection according to the voltage height, each powered by a standard triphase IGBT inverter module. Thus a high fault-tolerance is being achieved and the output transformer requirement is eliminated. A staggered space vector modulation (SSVM) technique applicable to triphase cascaded VSI topologies is also demonstrated. Both TC-VSI and MM-MI computer simulations and experimental tests demonstrate the feasibility of the systems",

      "abstract" : "The influence of an intravenous injection of chicken growth hormone (cGH), a total chicken pars distalis (PD) extract, and a PD extract depleted of cGH by immunoadsorption was studied in the 18-d-old chick embryo. Plasma concentrations of triiodothyronine (T3), thyroxine (T4), and hepatic 5'-monodeiodination (5'-D) activity were measured. An injection of total PD extract raised plasma T3, T4, and 5'-D activity, whereas a PD extract depleted of GH only increased plasma T4. The amount of cGH present in the PD extracts, as measured by homologous cGH radioimmunoassay, increased T3 and raised liver 5'-D, but had no effect on plasma T4. The effect on liver 5'-D was more pronounced with cGH than with a total PD extract, whereas the effect on plasma T3 was somewhat less pronounced. It was concluded that cGH increased the peripheral conversion of T4 into T3 in the chick embryo, whereas a PD extract depleted of cGH was purely thyrotropic. The PD extract also seemed to have 5'-D-suppressing activity.",

1.4.3. Find By Id In

This will find a list of organizations based on the organization ids provided as a parameter as shown in Request Parameters. The json response will have the specific organizations as shown in the Sample Response.

Request Parameters
Parameter Description

+ids+

The Organization ids.
Sample Request
GET /organizations/search/findByIdIn?ids=nbc8951b7%2Cn157a64e9%2Cna7893461 HTTP/1.1
Host: localhost:8080

1.4.4. Search

This search will return a json response listing all the organizations, based on the query parameters as shown in Request Parameters.

Request Parameters
Parameter Description

+query+

The search query

+facets+

The facet fields

+type.limit+

Type facet limit

+type.offset+

Type facet offset

+type.sort+

Type facet sort {index/count}

+page+

The page number

+size+

The page size

+sort+

The page sort field,{asc/desc}
Response Fields
Path Type Description

+_embedded.organizations+

+Array+

An array of Organization resources.

+_links+

+Object+

Links to other resources.

+page+

+Object+

Page details for Organization resources.

+facets+

+Array+

Facets for Organization resources.
Sample Request
GET /organizations/search/facet?query=*&facets=type&type.limit=5&type.offset=0&type.sort=COUNT&page=0&size=20&sort=id HTTP/1.1
Host: localhost:8080
Sample Response
HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Pragma: no-cache
X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
Expires: 0
X-Frame-Options: DENY
X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
Content-Type: application/hal+json;charset=UTF-8
Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, max-age=0, must-revalidate
Content-Length: 8014

    } ]
  },
  "_links" : {
    "self" : {
      "href" : "http://localhost:8080/organizations/search/facet?page=1&size=20&sort=id,asc"
    }
  },
  "facets" : [ {
    "field" : "type",
    "entries" : [ {
      "value" : "academicdepartment",
      "count" : 1
    }, {
      "value" : "organization",
      "count" : 1
    }, {
      "value" : "otheruniversity",
      "count" : 1
    }, {
      "value" : "publisher",
      "count" : 1
    } ]
  } ],
  "page" : {
    "size" : 20,
    "totalElements" : 3,
    "totalPages" : 1,
    "number" : 1
  }
}
CURL Sample
$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/organizations/search/facet?query=*&facets=type&type.limit=5&type.offset=0&type.sort=COUNT&page=0&size=20&sort=id' -i -X GET

1.4.5. Count

This count will return a json response containing the count, based on the query parameters as shown in Request Parameters.

Request Parameters
Parameter Description

+query+

The search query
Response Fields
Path Type Description

+value+

+Number+

The resulting count.
Sample Request
GET /organizations/search/count?query=* HTTP/1.1
Host: localhost:8080
Sample Response
HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Pragma: no-cache
X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
Expires: 0
X-Frame-Options: DENY
X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
Content-Length: 17
Content-Type: application/json;charset=UTF-8
Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, max-age=0, must-revalidate

{
  "value" : 3
}
CURL Sample
$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/organizations/search/count?query=*' -i -X GET

1.5. Persons

1.5.1. Directory

This provides a directory listing view of all the persons present in the system, based on the request parameters as shown.

Request Parameters
Parameter Description

+page+

The page number.

+size+

The page size.

+sort+

The page sort [field,asc/desc].
Response Fields
Path Type Description

+_embedded.persons+

+Array+

An array of Person resources.

+_links+

+Object+

Links to other resources.

+page+

+Object+

Page details for Person resources.

+facets+

+Array+

Facets for Person resources.
Sample Request
GET /persons?page=0&size=20&sort=id HTTP/1.1
Host: localhost:8080
Sample Response
HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Pragma: no-cache
X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
Expires: 0
X-Frame-Options: DENY
X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
Content-Length: 118370
Content-Type: application/hal+json;charset=UTF-8
Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, max-age=0, must-revalidate

      "overview" : "Dr. Vemulapalli's research is primarily focused on the development of recombinant vaccines against infectious diseases.  One of the targets of his vaccine research is  brucellosis, a bacterial zoonotic disease caused by certain members of the genus Brucella.  Brucellosis is a great concern to public health in developing countries due to widespread prevalence of Brucella infections in livestock.  In the US, reservoirs of Brucella infections in wildlife, such as bison, elk, and feral swine, continue to pose a threat to livestock industries and human health.  The currently available brucellosis veterinary vaccines are neither efficacious in wild animals nor safe for human use.  Dr. Vemulapalli has developed novel recombinant vaccine strains that showed dramatically enhanced vaccine efficacy against brucellosis in murine models.  Testing these vaccines in domestic and wild animals is a goal of his research program.  Research projects in his laboratory are aimed at 1) understanding the pathogenic mechanisms of Brucella species, 2) developing attenuated Brucella strains as vectors to deliver protective proteins of other pathogens and tumors, 3) developing recombinant subunit vaccines to porcine reproductive and respiratory syndrome virus, and 4) development of molecular diagnostics assays for infectious disease investigations.",

1.5.2. Find By Id

This will find a person based on the person id provided as a parameter as shown in Path Parameters. The json response will have the specific person as shown in the Sample Response.

Path Parameters
Table 5. /persons/{id}
Parameter Description

+id+

The Person id.

      "overview" : "Dr. Vemulapalli's research is primarily focused on the development of recombinant vaccines against infectious diseases.  One of the targets of his vaccine research is  brucellosis, a bacterial zoonotic disease caused by certain members of the genus Brucella.  Brucellosis is a great concern to public health in developing countries due to widespread prevalence of Brucella infections in livestock.  In the US, reservoirs of Brucella infections in wildlife, such as bison, elk, and feral swine, continue to pose a threat to livestock industries and human health.  The currently available brucellosis veterinary vaccines are neither efficacious in wild animals nor safe for human use.  Dr. Vemulapalli has developed novel recombinant vaccine strains that showed dramatically enhanced vaccine efficacy against brucellosis in murine models.  Testing these vaccines in domestic and wild animals is a goal of his research program.  Research projects in his laboratory are aimed at 1) understanding the pathogenic mechanisms of Brucella species, 2) developing attenuated Brucella strains as vectors to deliver protective proteins of other pathogens and tumors, 3) developing recombinant subunit vaccines to porcine reproductive and respiratory syndrome virus, and 4) development of molecular diagnostics assays for infectious disease investigations.",

CURL Sample
$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/persons/search/findByIdIn?ids=n163f68fe%2Cn5889f585%2Cn3e016f20' -i -X GET

1.5.4. Search

This search will return a json response listing all the persons, based on the query parameters as shown in Request Parameters.

Request Parameters
Parameter Description

+query+

The search query

+facets+

The facet fields

+type.limit+

Type facet limit

+type.offset+

Type facet offset

+type.sort+

Type facet sort {index/count}

+page+

The page number

+size+

The page size

+sort+

The page sort field,{asc/desc}
Response Fields
Path Type Description

+_embedded.persons+

+Array+

An array of Person resources.

+_links+

+Object+

Links to other resources.

+page+

+Object+

Page details for Person resources.

+facets+

+Array+

Facets for Person resources.
Sample Request
GET /persons/search/facet?query=*&facets=type&type.limit=5&type.offset=0&type.sort=COUNT&page=0&size=20&sort=id HTTP/1.1
Host: localhost:8080

      "overview" : "Dr. Vemulapalli's research is primarily focused on the development of recombinant vaccines against infectious diseases.  One of the targets of his vaccine research is  brucellosis, a bacterial zoonotic disease caused by certain members of the genus Brucella.  Brucellosis is a great concern to public health in developing countries due to widespread prevalence of Brucella infections in livestock.  In the US, reservoirs of Brucella infections in wildlife, such as bison, elk, and feral swine, continue to pose a threat to livestock industries and human health.  The currently available brucellosis veterinary vaccines are neither efficacious in wild animals nor safe for human use.  Dr. Vemulapalli has developed novel recombinant vaccine strains that showed dramatically enhanced vaccine efficacy against brucellosis in murine models.  Testing these vaccines in domestic and wild animals is a goal of his research program.  Research projects in his laboratory are aimed at 1) understanding the pathogenic mechanisms of Brucella species, 2) developing attenuated Brucella strains as vectors to deliver protective proteins of other pathogens and tumors, 3) developing recombinant subunit vaccines to porcine reproductive and respiratory syndrome virus, and 4) development of molecular diagnostics assays for infectious disease investigations.",

1.5.5. Count

This count will return a json response containing the count, based on the query parameters as shown in Request Parameters.

Request Parameters
Parameter Description

+query+

The search query
Response Fields
Path Type Description

+value+

+Number+

The resulting count.
Sample Request
GET /persons/search/count?query=* HTTP/1.1
Host: localhost:8080
Sample Response
HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Pragma: no-cache
X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
Expires: 0
X-Frame-Options: DENY
X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
Content-Length: 17
Content-Type: application/json;charset=UTF-8
Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, max-age=0, must-revalidate

{
  "value" : 3
}
CURL Sample
$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/persons/search/count?query=*' -i -X GET

1.6. Processes

1.6.1. Directory

This provides a directory listing view of all the processes present in the system, based on the request parameters as shown.

Request Parameters
Parameter Description

+page+

The page number.

+size+

The page size.

+sort+

The page sort [field,asc/desc].
Response Fields
Path Type Description

+_embedded.processes+

+Array+

An array of Process resources.

+_links+

+Object+

Links to other resources.

+page+

+Object+

Page details for Process resources.

+facets+

+Array+

Facets for Process resources.
Sample Request
GET /processes?page=0&size=20&sort=id HTTP/1.1
Host: localhost:8080
Sample Response
HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Pragma: no-cache
X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
Expires: 0
X-Frame-Options: DENY
X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
Content-Type: application/hal+json;charset=UTF-8
Content-Length: 2263
Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, max-age=0, must-revalidate

Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, max-age=0, must-revalidate

{
  "value" : 3
}
CURL Sample
$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/relationships/search/count?query=*' -i -X GET

2. Registration

This endpoint helps an expertise/scholar to create his/her profile using this system.

2.1. Submit

User is required to enter first name, last name and an email address to submit the registration form. This creates a new token and an email, using the email address provided in the registraion form, is sent to the user. A new user object is then created with a specific role assigned. Clicking on the email link will confirm the user’s email provided.

2.1.1. Request Parameters

Path Type Description

+firstName+

+String+

The first name of the registered account. Size must be between 2 and 64 inclusive.

+lastName+

+String+

The last name of the registered account. Size must be between 2 and 64 inclusive.

+email+

+String+

The e-mail address of the registered account.

2.1.2. Sample Request

POST /registration HTTP/1.1
Content-Length: 72
Content-Type: application/json;charset=UTF-8
Host: localhost:8080

{"firstName":"Bob","lastName":"Boring","email":"bboring@mailinator.com"}

2.1.3. Sample Response

HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Pragma: no-cache
X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
Expires: 0
X-Frame-Options: DENY
X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
Content-Length: 72
Content-Type: application/json;charset=UTF-8
Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, max-age=0, must-revalidate

{"firstName":"Bob","lastName":"Boring","email":"bboring@mailinator.com"}

2.1.4. CURL Sample

$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/registration' -i -X POST \
    -H 'Content-Type: application/json;charset=UTF-8' \
    -d '{"firstName":"Bob","lastName":"Boring","email":"bboring@mailinator.com"}'

2.2. Confirm

This endpoint requires a key string, (obtained when the user clicks on the email confirmation link) which verifies the user token. This key string constructs a token by obtaining user-specified extended information associated with the token, when it was first created. If the user is found and the token is not expired, a user object (as shown in "Sample Response") is returned.

2.2.1. Request Parameters

Parameter Description

+key+

The registration verification key.

2.2.2. Sample Request

GET /registration?key=bboring%40mailinator.com HTTP/1.1
Host: localhost:8080

2.2.3. Sample Response

HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Pragma: no-cache
X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
Expires: 0
X-Frame-Options: DENY
X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
Content-Length: 72
Content-Type: application/json;charset=UTF-8
Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, max-age=0, must-revalidate

{"firstName":"Bob","lastName":"Boring","email":"bboring@mailinator.com"}

2.2.4. CURL Sample

$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/registration?key=bboring%40mailinator.com' -i -X GET

2.3. Complete

This endpoint requires the registration object. Once the user creates a new password and confirms it, the user object is constructed using the email from the registration object. If the account is found, then this endpoint will return a user with an enabled account.

2.3.1. Request Parameters

Path Type Description

+firstName+

+String+

The first name of the registered account. Size must be between 2 and 64 inclusive.

+lastName+

+String+

The last name of the registered account. Size must be between 2 and 64 inclusive.

+email+

+String+

The e-mail address of the registered account.

+password+

+String+

The password for the registered account.

+confirm+

+String+

The password confirmation, which should match the password.

2.3.2. Sample Request

PUT /registration HTTP/1.1
Content-Length: 127
Content-Type: application/json;charset=UTF-8
Host: localhost:8080

{"firstName":"Bob","lastName":"Boring","email":"bboring@mailinator.com","password":"HelloWorld123!","confirm":"HelloWorld123!"}

2.3.3. Sample Response

HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Pragma: no-cache
X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
Expires: 0
X-Frame-Options: DENY
X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
Content-Type: application/json;charset=UTF-8
Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, max-age=0, must-revalidate
Content-Length: 134

{"id":2,"firstName":"Bob","lastName":"Boring","email":"bboring@mailinator.com","role":"ROLE_SUPER_ADMIN","active":true,"enabled":true}

2.3.4. CURL Sample

$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/registration' -i -X PUT \
    -H 'Content-Type: application/json;charset=UTF-8' \
    -d '{"firstName":"Bob","lastName":"Boring","email":"bboring@mailinator.com","password":"HelloWorld123!","confirm":"HelloWorld123!"}'

3. Login

This endpoint allows the registered user to log in using his/her username and password.

3.1. Request Parameters

Parameter Description

+username+

The username to login as, usually an e-mail address.

+password+

The password associated with the specified username.

3.2. Response Fields

Path Type Description

+id+

+Number+

The ID of the user.

+firstName+

+String+

The first name of the user. Must not be null. Size must be between 2 and 64 inclusive.

+lastName+

+String+

The last name of the user. Must not be null. Size must be between 2 and 64 inclusive.

+email+

+String+

The e-mail address of the user. Must be a well-formed email address. Must not be null.

+role+

+String+

The authorization role of the user. Must not be null.

+active+

+Boolean+

The expired/unexpired status of the user.

+enabled+

+Boolean+

The locked/unlocked status of the user.

3.3. Sample Request

POST /login HTTP/1.1
Host: localhost:8080
Content-Type: application/x-www-form-urlencoded

username=bboring%40mailinator.com&password=HelloWorld123%21

3.4. Sample Response

HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Pragma: no-cache
X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
Expires: 0
X-Frame-Options: DENY
X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
Content-Length: 127
Content-Type: application/json;charset=UTF-8
Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, max-age=0, must-revalidate
Set-Cookie: SESSION=MjNhNWY4MjUtOTU4My00OGEyLWJhYjgtZWRjOTM0YjAyMzY0; Path=/; SameSite=Lax

{"id":2,"firstName":"Bob","lastName":"Boring","email":"bboring@mailinator.com","role":"ROLE_USER","active":true,"enabled":true}

3.5. CURL Sample

$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/login' -i -X POST \
    -d 'username=bboring%40mailinator.com&password=HelloWorld123%21'

4. Logout

This endpoint allows the authenticated user to log out.

4.1. Sample Request

POST /logout HTTP/1.1
Host: localhost:8080
Cookie: SESSION=YmEzNTBhYmQtYTk1Yy00NDBhLWIyNTUtNThjZmFhYjBlNWVl

4.2. Sample Response

HTTP/1.1 205 Reset Content
Pragma: no-cache
X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
Expires: 0
X-Frame-Options: DENY
Set-Cookie: remove=; Path=/; Max-Age=0; Expires=Thu, 01 Jan 1970 00:00:00 GMT
Set-Cookie: SESSION=; Path=/; Max-Age=0; Expires=Thu, 01 Jan 1970 00:00:00 GMT; SameSite=Lax
Set-Cookie: SESSION=; Path=/; Max-Age=0; Expires=Thu, 01 Jan 1970 00:00:00 GMT; SameSite=Lax
X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
Content-Length: 7
Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, max-age=0, must-revalidate

Success

4.3. CURL Sample

$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/logout' -i -X POST \
    --cookie 'SESSION=YmEzNTBhYmQtYTk1Yy00NDBhLWIyNTUtNThjZmFhYjBlNWVl'

5. User

This endpoint returns the authenticated user.

5.1. Response Fields

Path Type Description

+id+

+Number+

The ID of the user.

+firstName+

+String+

The first name of the user. Must not be null. Size must be between 2 and 64 inclusive.

+lastName+

+String+

The last name of the user. Must not be null. Size must be between 2 and 64 inclusive.

+email+

+String+

The e-mail address of the user. Must be a well-formed email address. Must not be null.

+role+

+String+

The authorization role of the user. Must not be null.

+active+

+Boolean+

The expired/unexpired status of the user.

+enabled+

+Boolean+

The locked/unlocked status of the user.

5.2. Sample Request

GET /user HTTP/1.1
Host: localhost:8080
Cookie: SESSION=ZGYzYmRlZTctYTAyOC00MDI5LWE4YzctYmU0ZmYzOWYwMjJh

5.3. Sample Response

HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Pragma: no-cache
X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
Expires: 0
X-Frame-Options: DENY
X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
Content-Type: application/json;charset=UTF-8
Content-Length: 129
Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, max-age=0, must-revalidate

{"id":18,"firstName":"Bob","lastName":"Boring","email":"bboring@mailinator.com","role":"ROLE_ADMIN","active":true,"enabled":true}

5.4. CURL Sample

$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/user' -i -X GET \
    --cookie 'SESSION=ZGYzYmRlZTctYTAyOC00MDI5LWE4YzctYmU0ZmYzOWYwMjJh'

6. Administration

6.1. Directory Views

This section describes about the directory views of the application. This object is a persistent representation of a directory UI.

6.1.1. Directory

This displays a list of all the directory view objects based on parameters like page, size or sort feature based on name, collection etc as shown in Request Parameters.

Request Parameters
Parameter Description

+page+

The page number.

+size+

The page size.

+sort+

The page sort.
Response Fields
Path Type Description

+_embedded.directoryViews+

+Array+

An array of Directory View resources.

+_links+

+Object+

Links to other resources.

+page+

+Object+

Page details for Directory View resources.
Sample Request
GET /directoryViews?page=0&size=20&sort=name HTTP/1.1
Host: localhost:8080
Sample Response
HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Pragma: no-cache
X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
Expires: 0
X-Frame-Options: DENY
X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
Content-Type: application/hal+json;charset=UTF-8
Content-Length: 1324
Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, max-age=0, must-revalidate

{
  "_embedded" : {
    "directoryViews" : [ {
      "name" : "People",
      "collection" : "persons",
      "layout" : "LIST",
      "templates" : {
        "default" : "<h1>Person template from WSYWIG</h1>"
      },
      "styles" : [ "color: maroon;" ],
      "facets" : [ {
        "name" : "Name",
        "field" : "name",
        "type" : "STRING",
        "sort" : "COUNT",
        "direction" : "DESC",
        "limit" : 20,
        "collapsed" : true,
        "hidden" : false
      } ],
      "filters" : [ {
        "field" : "type",
        "value" : "FacultyMember"
      } ],
      "sort" : [ {
        "field" : "name",
        "direction" : "ASC",
        "date" : false
      } ],
      "index" : {
        "field" : "name",
        "operationKey" : "ENDS_WITH",
        "options" : [ ]
      },
      "_links" : {
        "self" : {
          "href" : "http://localhost:8080/directoryViews/3"
        },
        "directoryView" : {
          "href" : "http://localhost:8080/directoryViews/3"
        }
      }
    } ]
  },
  "_links" : {
    "self" : {
      "href" : "http://localhost:8080/directoryViews"
    },
    "profile" : {
      "href" : "http://localhost:8080/profile/directoryViews"
    }
  },
  "page" : {
    "size" : 20,
    "totalElements" : 1,
    "totalPages" : 1,
    "number" : 1
  }
}
CURL Sample
$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/directoryViews?page=0&size=20&sort=name' -i -X GET

6.1.3. Delete

A directory view can be deleted by passing the directoryView id as a path parameter. This will return a NO_CONTENT (204) http status code as shown in the Sample Response.

Path Parameters
Table 8. /directoryViews/{id}
Parameter Description

+id+

The Directory View id
Sample Request
DELETE /directoryViews/1 HTTP/1.1
Host: localhost:8080
Cookie: SESSION=NGYxM2MxYWQtYTY0MC00ZTY2LWFhNDMtYjE2OTg4MTEzNGI5
Sample Response
HTTP/1.1 204 No Content
Pragma: no-cache
X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
Expires: 0
X-Frame-Options: DENY
X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, max-age=0, must-revalidate
CURL Sample
$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/directoryViews/1' -i -X DELETE \
    --cookie 'SESSION=NGYxM2MxYWQtYTY0MC00ZTY2LWFhNDMtYjE2OTg4MTEzNGI5'

6.2. Discovery Views

This section describes about the discovery views of the application. This object is a persistent representation of a discovery view.

6.2.1. Directory

This displays a list of all the discovery view objects based on parameters like page, size or sort feature based on name, collection etc as shown in Request Parameters.

Request Parameters
Parameter Description

+page+

The page number.

+size+

The page size.

+sort+

The page sort.
Response Fields
Path Type Description

+_embedded.discoveryViews+

+Array+

An array of Discovery View resources.

+_links+

+Object+

Links to other resources.

+page+

+Object+

Page details for Discovery View resources.
Sample Request
GET /discoveryViews?page=0&size=20&sort=name HTTP/1.1
Host: localhost:8080
Sample Response
HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Pragma: no-cache
Content-Length: 1209
X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
Expires: 0
X-Frame-Options: DENY
X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
Content-Type: application/hal+json;charset=UTF-8
Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, max-age=0, must-revalidate

{
  "_embedded" : {
    "discoveryViews" : [ {
      "name" : "People",
      "collection" : "persons",
      "layout" : "GRID",
      "templates" : {
        "default" : "<h1>Person template from WSYWIG</h1>"
      },
      "styles" : [ "color: maroon;" ],
      "facets" : [ {
        "name" : "Name",
        "field" : "name",
        "type" : "STRING",
        "sort" : "COUNT",
        "direction" : "DESC",
        "limit" : 20,
        "collapsed" : true,
        "hidden" : false
      } ],
      "filters" : [ {
        "field" : "type",
        "value" : "FacultyMember"
      } ],

        "field" : "name",
        "direction" : "ASC",
        "date" : false
      } ],
      "_links" : {
        "self" : {
          "href" : "http://localhost:8080/discoveryViews/4"
        },
        "discoveryView" : {
          "href" : "http://localhost:8080/discoveryViews/4"
        }
      }
    } ]

    "self" : {
      "href" : "http://localhost:8080/discoveryViews"

Path Type Description

+String+

+layout+

+String+

The layout of the Discovery View.

+templates+

+Object+

The result templates of the Discovery View.

+styles+

+Array+

An array of result style strings of the Discovery View.

+facets+

+Array+

An array of Facet resources.

+filters+

+Array+

An array of Filters resources.

+sort+

+Array+

An array of Sort resources.

6.2.3. Delete

A discovery view can be deleted by passing the discoveryView id as a path parameter. This will return a NO_CONTENT (204) http status code as shown in the Sample Response.

Path Parameters
Table 12. /discoveryViews/{id}
Parameter Description

+id+

The Discovery View id
Sample Request
DELETE /discoveryViews/1 HTTP/1.1
Host: localhost:8080
Cookie: SESSION=MjJmMDNiZjctYmYyNC00YTg4LWIwOWQtZDM5MjZjYTlhMGVm
Sample Response
HTTP/1.1 204 No Content
Pragma: no-cache
X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
Expires: 0
X-Frame-Options: DENY
X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, max-age=0, must-revalidate
CURL Sample
$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/discoveryViews/1' -i -X DELETE \
    --cookie 'SESSION=MjJmMDNiZjctYmYyNC00YTg4LWIwOWQtZDM5MjZjYTlhMGVm'

6.3.3. Delete

A display view can be deleted by passing the displayView id as a path parameter. This will return a NO_CONTENT (204) http status code as shown in the Sample Response.

Path Parameters
Table 16. /displayViews/{id}
Parameter Description

+id+

The Display View id
Sample Request
DELETE /displayViews/1 HTTP/1.1
Host: localhost:8080
Cookie: SESSION=MzQ5N2FkMzgtZmYyMS00NTkwLTgwMGQtODg5NmFiOGQ1Y2Rh
Sample Response
HTTP/1.1 204 No Content
Pragma: no-cache
X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
Expires: 0
X-Frame-Options: DENY
X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, max-age=0, must-revalidate
CURL Sample
$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/displayViews/1' -i -X DELETE \
    --cookie 'SESSION=MzQ5N2FkMzgtZmYyMS00NTkwLTgwMGQtODg5NmFiOGQ1Y2Rh'

6.4. Themes

This section describes about the "look and feel" of the application. This object is a collection of properties like the header, logo, footer, color, size, styles etc. The default theme view is seen in the Sample Response.

6.4.1. Directory

This displays a list of all the theme objects based on parameters like page, size or sort feature based on name, organization etc as shown in Request Parameters.

Request Parameters
Parameter Description

+page+

The page number.

+size+

The page size.

+sort+

The page sort.
Response Fields
Path Type Description

+_embedded.themes+

An array of Theme resources.

+_links+

+Object+

Links to other resources.

+page+

+Object+

Page details for Theme resources.

  "name" : "Test",
  "organization" : "Testing Limited",
  "active" : true,
  "home" : {
    "heroesNavigable" : false,
    "heroes" : [ {
      "imageUri" : "/assets/images/hero.png",
      "imageAlt" : "Hero",
      "watermarkImageUri" : "/assets/images/watermark.png",
      "watermarkText" : "Watermark",
      "baseText" : "This is only a test!",
      "fontColor" : "#ffffff",
      "linkColor" : "#000000",
      "linkHoverColor" : "#ffc222",
      "slideInterval" : 5000
    } ],
    "variables" : [ {
      "key" : "--test",
      "value" : "home"
    } ]
  },
  "header" : {
    "navbar" : {
      "brandText" : "Hello, World!",
      "brandUri" : "http://localhost:4200",
      "logoUri" : "/assets/images/logo.png",
      "links" : [ {
        "label" : "Home",
        "uri" : "http://localhost:4200"
      } ],
      "variables" : [ {
        "key" : "--test",
        "value" : "navbar"
      } ]
    },
    "banner" : {
      "imageUri" : "/assets/images/banner.png",
      "altText" : "Tested",
      "variables" : [ {
        "key" : "--test",
        "value" : "banner"
      } ]
    },
    "variables" : [ {
      "key" : "--test",
      "value" : "header"
    } ]
  },
  "footer" : {
    "links" : [ {
      "label" : "About",
      "uri" : "http://localhost:4200/about"
    } ],
    "variables" : [ {
      "key" : "--test",
      "value" : "footer"
    } ]
  },
  "colors" : [ {
    "key" : "--red",
    "value" : "#ff0000"
  }, {
    "key" : "--green",
    "value" : "#00ff00"
  }, {
    "key" : "--blue",
    "value" : "#0000ff"
  } ],
  "variants" : [ {
    "key" : "--primary",
    "value" : "#007bff"
  }, {
    "key" : "--secondary",
    "value" : "#6c757d"
  }, {
    "key" : "--success",
    "value" : "#28a745"
  } ],
  "variables" : [ {
    "key" : "--accent",
    "value" : "#ffc222"
  }, {
    "key" : "--navigation-color",
    "value" : "#3c0000"
  }, {
    "key" : "--navbar-color",
    "value" : "#ffffff"
  } ],
  "_links" : {
    "self" : {
      "href" : "http://localhost:8080/themes/11"
    },
    "theme" : {
      "href" : "http://localhost:8080/themes/11"
    }
  }
}
CURL Sample
$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/themes/search/active' -i -X GET

6.4.3. Create

A theme is created by adding a fields like name, organization, header, footer etc along with other styling variables as shown in the Request Parameters. A theme when created, by default, has the active check set to false. This boolean flag, when checked will activate the specific theme.

Request Fields
Path Type Description

+active+

+Boolean+

Designates the theme currently in use.

+name+

+String+

The name of the theme. Must not be null. Size must be between 2 and 64 inclusive.

+organization+

+String+

An organization the theme belongs to.

+home+

+Object+

A Home resource.

+header+

+Object+

A Header resource.

+footer+

+Object+

A Footer resource.

+colors+

+Array+

An array of Color resources.

+variants+

+Array+

An array of Variants resources.

+variables+

+Array+

An array of Variables resources.
Response Fields
Path Type Description

+active+

+Boolean+

Designates the theme currently in use.

+name+

+String+

The name of the theme. Must not be null. Size must be between 2 and 64 inclusive.

+organization+

+String+

An organization the theme belongs to.

+home+

+Object+

A Home resource.

+header+

+Object+

A Header resource.

+footer+

+Object+

A Footer resource.

+colors+

+Array+

An array of Color resources.

+variants+

+Array+

An array of Variants resources.

+variables+

+Array+

An array of Variables resources.

+_links+

+Object+

Links to other resources.

6.4.4. Delete

A theme can be deleted by passing the theme id as a path parameter. The active flag has to be set to false prior to delete. This will return a NO_CONTENT (204) http status code as shown in the Sample Response.

Path Parameters
Table 20. /themes/{id}
Parameter Description

+id+

The Theme id
Sample Request
DELETE /themes/3 HTTP/1.1
Host: localhost:8080
Cookie: SESSION=MzA2MTY0YjctNDUwNC00Y2Q1LWJjNGYtYWRlNzVkMjU3NGI1
Sample Response
HTTP/1.1 204 No Content
Pragma: no-cache
X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
Expires: 0
X-Frame-Options: DENY
X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, max-age=0, must-revalidate
CURL Sample
$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/themes/3' -i -X DELETE \
    --cookie 'SESSION=MzA2MTY0YjctNDUwNC00Y2Q1LWJjNGYtYWRlNzVkMjU3NGI1'

A Home resource.

A Header resource.

A Footer resource.

An array of Color resources.

+variants+

An array of Variants resources.

An array of Variables resources.

+Boolean+

Designates the theme currently in use.

      "key" : "--test",
      "value" : "home"
    } ]
  },
  "header" : {
    "navbar" : {
      "brandText" : "Hello, World!",
      "brandUri" : "http://localhost:4200",
      "logoUri" : "/assets/images/logo.png",
      "links" : [ {
        "label" : "Home",
        "uri" : "http://localhost:4200"
      } ],
      "variables" : [ {
        "key" : "--test",
        "value" : "navbar"
      } ]
    },
    "banner" : {
      "imageUri" : "/assets/images/banner.png",
      "altText" : "Tested",
      "variables" : [ {

        "value" : "banner"
      } ]

    "variables" : [ {
      "key" : "--test",
      "value" : "header"
    } ]

  "footer" : {

      "label" : "About",

$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/themes/6' -i -X PUT \
    --cookie 'SESSION=MmNlMzQyOGItOWZlZS00NDY2LWE4Y2UtMTU3NDQwZDIxYjEx' \
    -d '{"id":6,"name":"Test","organization":"Testing Limited","active":true,"home":{"heroesNavigable":false,"heroes":[{"imageUri":"/assets/images/hero.png","imageAlt":"Hero","watermarkImageUri":"/assets/images/watermark.png","watermarkText":"Watermark","baseText":"This is only a test!","fontColor":"#ffffff","linkColor":"#000000","linkHoverColor":"#ffc222","slideInterval":5000}],"variables":[{"key":"--test","value":"home"}]},"header":{"navbar":{"brandText":"Hello, World!","brandUri":"http://localhost:4200","logoUri":"/assets/images/logo.png","links":[{"label":"Home","uri":"http://localhost:4200"}],"variables":[{"key":"--test","value":"navbar"}]},"banner":{"imageUri":"/assets/images/banner.png","altText":"Tested","variables":[{"key":"--test","value":"banner"}]},"variables":[{"key":"--test","value":"header"}]},"footer":{"links":[{"label":"About","uri":"http://localhost:4200/about"}],"variables":[{"key":"--test","value":"footer"}]},"colors":[{"key":"--red","value":"#ff0000"},{"key":"--green","value":"#00ff00"},{"key":"--blue","value":"#0000ff"}],"variants":[{"key":"--primary","value":"#007bff"},{"key":"--secondary","value":"#6c757d"},{"key":"--success","value":"#28a745"}],"variables":[{"key":"--accent","value":"#ffc222"},{"key":"--navigation-color","value":"#3c0000"},{"key":"--navbar-color","value":"#ffffff"}]}'

6.5. Users

This sections describes the list of users present in the system - faculty and non faculty.

6.5.1. Directory

This displays a list of all the users based on parameters like page, size or sort feature based on name, organization etc as shown in Request Parameters.

Request Parameters
Parameter Description

+page+

The page number.

+size+

The page size.

+sort+

The page sort.
Response Fields
Path Type Description

+_embedded.users+

+Array+

An array of User resources.

+_links+

+Object+

Links to other resources.

+page+

+Object+

Page details for User resources.
Sample Request
GET /users?page=0&size=20&sort=id HTTP/1.1
Host: localhost:8080
Cookie: SESSION=NmU2NjVmMDItOWZhMC00NGZhLWJjMDMtNTQzZWNiM2RmN2Y2
Sample Response
HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Pragma: no-cache
X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
Content-Length: 682
Expires: 0
X-Frame-Options: DENY
X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
Content-Type: application/hal+json;charset=UTF-8
Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, max-age=0, must-revalidate

{
  "_embedded" : {
    "users" : [ {
      "firstName" : "Eddie",
      "lastName" : "Exciting",
      "email" : "eexciting@mailinator.com",
      "role" : "ROLE_ADMIN",
      "active" : true,
      "enabled" : true,
      "_links" : {
        "self" : {
          "href" : "http://localhost:8080/users/5"
        },
        "user" : {
          "href" : "http://localhost:8080/users/5"
        }
      }
    } ]
  },
  "_links" : {
    "self" : {
      "href" : "http://localhost:8080/users"
    },
    "profile" : {
      "href" : "http://localhost:8080/profile/users"
    }
  },
  "page" : {
    "size" : 20,
    "totalElements" : 1,
    "totalPages" : 1,
    "number" : 1
  }
}
CURL Sample
$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/users?page=0&size=20&sort=id' -i -X GET \
    --cookie 'SESSION=NmU2NjVmMDItOWZhMC00NGZhLWJjMDMtNTQzZWNiM2RmN2Y2'

6.5.2. Delete

A user can be deleted by providing the user id in the path parameters as shown. If successful, the response will be a json response (as shown in the Sample Response).

Path Parameters
Table 24. /users/{id}
Parameter Description

+id+

The User ID.
Sample Request
DELETE /users/13 HTTP/1.1
Content-Length: 38
Host: localhost:8080
Cookie: SESSION=ZTA2MzkxOTctZWNhOC00YjM4LWJiZmYtMmM2OWJlN2E0OTZj

{"role": "ROLE_USER", "active": false}
Sample Response
HTTP/1.1 204 No Content
Pragma: no-cache
X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
Expires: 0
X-Frame-Options: DENY
X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, max-age=0, must-revalidate
CURL Sample
$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/users/13' -i -X DELETE \
    --cookie 'SESSION=ZTA2MzkxOTctZWNhOC00YjM4LWJiZmYtMmM2OWJlN2E0OTZj' \
    -d '{"role": "ROLE_USER", "active": false}'

6.5.3. Find by ID

An admin user can find a specific user by providing user id in the path parameters as shown. If successful, the json response will be as shown in the Sample Response.

Path Parameters
Table 25. /users/{id}
Parameter Description

+id+

The User ID.
Response Fields
Path Type Description

+firstName+

+String+

The first name of the user. Must not be null. Size must be between 2 and 64 inclusive.

+lastName+

+String+

The last name of the user. Must not be null. Size must be between 2 and 64 inclusive.

+email+

+String+

The e-mail address of the user. Must be a well-formed email address. Must not be null.

+role+

+String+

The authorization role of the user. Must not be null.

+active+

+Boolean+

The expired/unexpired status of the user.

+enabled+

+Boolean+

The locked/unlocked status of the user.

+_links+

+Object+

Links to other resources.
Sample Request
GET /users/8 HTTP/1.1
Host: localhost:8080
Cookie: SESSION=NjVjYmIwYzEtYTE0ZC00ZjU4LWEyZWUtZGQzOWUxOWRiNjFl
Sample Response
HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Pragma: no-cache
X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
Expires: 0
X-Frame-Options: DENY
X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
Content-Type: application/hal+json;charset=UTF-8
Content-Length: 315
Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, max-age=0, must-revalidate

{
  "firstName" : "Eddie",
  "lastName" : "Exciting",
  "email" : "eexciting@mailinator.com",
  "role" : "ROLE_ADMIN",
  "active" : true,
  "enabled" : true,
  "_links" : {
    "self" : {
      "href" : "http://localhost:8080/users/8"
    },
    "user" : {
      "href" : "http://localhost:8080/users/8"
    }
  }
}
CURL Sample
$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/users/8' -i -X GET \
    --cookie 'SESSION=NjVjYmIwYzEtYTE0ZC00ZjU4LWEyZWUtZGQzOWUxOWRiNjFl'

6.5.4. Patch

An admin user can partially update specific fields in the user account by providing user id in the path parameters as shown. If successful, the json response will be an updated user profile as shown in the Sample Response.

Path Parameters
Table 26. /users/{id}
Parameter Description

+id+

The User ID.
Request Parameters
Parameter Description

+firstName+

The first name of the user. Must not be null. Size must be between 2 and 64 inclusive.

+lastName+

The last name of the user. Must not be null. Size must be between 2 and 64 inclusive.

+email+

The e-mail address of the user. Must be a well-formed email address. Must not be null.

+role+

The authorization role of the user. Must not be null.

+active+

The expired/unexpired status of the user.

+enabled+

The locked/unlocked status of the user.
Response Fields
Path Type Description

+firstName+

+String+

The first name of the user. Must not be null. Size must be between 2 and 64 inclusive.

+lastName+

+String+

The last name of the user. Must not be null. Size must be between 2 and 64 inclusive.

+email+

+String+

The e-mail address of the user. Must be a well-formed email address. Must not be null.

+role+

+String+

The authorization role of the user. Must not be null.

+active+

+Boolean+

The expired/unexpired status of the user.

+enabled+

+Boolean+

The locked/unlocked status of the user.

+_links+

+Object+

Links to other resources.
Sample Request
PATCH /users/9 HTTP/1.1
Content-Length: 38
Host: localhost:8080
Cookie: SESSION=NzJhMWE4MGYtNzY5Ny00YmY3LTljMTgtZmNhZDNlMjFiZDYx

{"role": "ROLE_USER", "active": false}
Sample Response
HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Pragma: no-cache
X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
Expires: 0
X-Frame-Options: DENY
X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
Content-Type: application/hal+json;charset=UTF-8
Content-Length: 315
Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, max-age=0, must-revalidate

{
  "firstName" : "Eddie",
  "lastName" : "Exciting",
  "email" : "eexciting@mailinator.com",
  "role" : "ROLE_USER",
  "active" : false,
  "enabled" : true,
  "_links" : {
    "self" : {
      "href" : "http://localhost:8080/users/9"
    },
    "user" : {
      "href" : "http://localhost:8080/users/9"
    }
  }
}
CURL Sample
$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/users/9' -i -X PATCH \
    --cookie 'SESSION=NzJhMWE4MGYtNzY5Ny00YmY3LTljMTgtZmNhZDNlMjFiZDYx' \
    -d '{"role": "ROLE_USER", "active": false}'
